    JDBC Introduction    &#x2022; JDBC provides a standard library for      accessing relational databases      &#x2013; API standardizes         &#x2022;   Way to establish connection to database         &#x2022;   Approach to initiating queries         &#x2022;   Method to create stored (parameterized) queries         &#x2022;   The data structure of query result (table)              &#x2013; Determining the number of columns              &#x2013; Looking up metadata, etc.      &#x2013; API does not standardize SQL syntax         &#x2022; You send strings; JDBC is not embedded SQL      &#x2013; JDBC classes are in the java.sql package      &#x2013; JDBC stands for &#x201C;Java DataBase Connectivity&#x201D;7 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-6-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 6 image" target="_blank">
        6.
      </a>
    On-line Resources    &#x2022; Sun&#x2019;s JDBC Site      &#x2013; http://java.sun.com/javase/6/docs/technotes/guides/jdbc/    &#x2022; JDBC Tutorial      &#x2013; http://java.sun.com/docs/books/tutorial/jdbc/    &#x2022; API for java.sql      &#x2013; http://java.sun.com/javase/6/docs/api/java/sql/        package-summary.html    &#x2022; List of Available JDBC Drivers      &#x2013; http://developers.sun.com/product/jdbc/drivers         &#x2022; Or, just look in your database vendor&#x2019;s documentation8 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">

        7.
      </a>
    JDBC Drivers    &#x2022; JDBC consists of two parts:      &#x2013; JDBC API, a purely                        Java Application        Java-based API      &#x2013; JDBC Driver Manager,which              JDBC API        communicates with                     JDBC Driver Manager        vendor-specific drivers that                                                    JDBC Driver API        perform the real communication        with the database.                  JDBC-ODBC                                              Bridge                                                               Vendor Specific                                                                 JDBC Driver         &#x2022; Point: translation to vendor           format is performed on           the client                      Vendor Specific        Database                                            ODBC Driver            &#x2013; No changes needed              to server            &#x2013; Driver (translator) needed    Database              on client9 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-8-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 8 image" target="_blank">

    JDBC Data Types      JDBC Type         Java Type     BIT             boolean     TINYINT         byte     SMALLINT        short     INTEGER         int     BIGINT          long           JDBC Type            Java Type     REAL            float          NUMERIC       BigDecimal     FLOAT           double         DECIMAL     DOUBLE                         DATE          java.sql.Date     BINARY          byte[]         TIME          java.sql.Timestamp     VARBINARY                      TIMESTAMP     LONGVARBINARY                  CLOB          Clob     CHAR            String                                    BLOB          Blob     VARCHAR                        ARRAY         Array     LONGVARCHAR                    DISTINCT      mapping of underlying type                                    STRUCT        Struct                                    REF           Ref                                    JAVA_OBJECT   underlying Java class10

    &#xA9; 2012 Marty HallSteps for Using JDBC               Customized Java EE Training: http://courses.coreservlets.com/Java, JSF 2, PrimeFaces, Servlets, JSP, Ajax, jQuery, Spring, Hibernate, RESTful Web Services, Hadoop, Android.   <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-10-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 10 image" target="_blank">
        10.
      </a>
    JDBC Design Strategies     &#x2022; In general, plan for changes to data access       &#x2013; Limit the data access to single area of code          &#x2022; Don&#x2019;t distribute JDBC calls throughout the code          &#x2022; Plan ahead for changing from JDBC to Hibernate or            another tool       &#x2013; Don&#x2019;t return JDBC-specific (or Hibernate-specific)         objects from the data-access layer          &#x2022; Return ordinary Java objects instead     &#x2022; In JDBC, plan for changes       &#x2013; Limit the definition of driver, URL, etc. to single location     &#x2022; Let database experts do their stuff       &#x2013; If database is complex, let database expert design the         database and design the queries12 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-11-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 11 image" target="_blank">
        11.
      </a>
    Seven Basic Steps in     Using JDBC     1. Load the driver          &#x2013;     Not required in Java 6, so Java 6 needs only 6 steps.     2.       Define the Connection URL     3.       Establish the Connection     4.       Create a Statement object     5.       Execute a query     6.       Process the results     7.       Close the connection13 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-12-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 12 image" target="_blank">
        12.
      </a>
    JDBC Step 1: Load the Driver     &#x2022; Not required in Java 6       &#x2013; In Java SE 6.0 and later (JDBC 4.0 and later), the driver         is loaded automatically.     &#x2022; Java 5 and earlier       &#x2013; Load the driver class only. The class has a static         initialization block that makes an instance and registers it         with the DriverManager.        try {          Class.forName("com.mysql.jdbc.Driver");          Class.forName("oracle.jdbc.driver.OracleDriver");        } catch (ClassNotFoundException cnfe) {          System.out.println("Error loading driver: " + cnfe);        }14 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-13-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 13 image" target="_blank">
        13.
      </a>
    JDBC Step 2: Define the     Connection URL     &#x2022; Remote databases       &#x2013; Format is &#x201C;jdbc:vendorName:&#x2026;&#x201D;          &#x2022; Address contains hostname, port, and database name          &#x2022; Exact details given by supplier of JDBC driver     &#x2022; Embedded Derby database       &#x2013; The &#x201C;Java DB&#x201D; (i.e., Apache Derby) is bundled with Java 6         and can be used for a database embedded in the same Java VM         that runs the app server.       &#x2013; Format is &#x201C;jdbc:derby:databaseName&#x201D;     &#x2022; Examples      String host = "dbhost.yourcompany.com";      String dbName = "someName";      int port = 1234;      String mySqlUrl = "jdbc:mysql//" + host + ":" + port +                        "/" + dbName;      String embeddedDerbyUrl = "jdbc:derby" + dbName;15 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-14-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 14 image" target="_blank">
        14.
      </a>
    JDBC Step 3: Establish the     Connection     &#x2022; Get the main connection        Properties userInfo = new Properties();        userInfo.put("user", "jay_debesee");        userInfo.put("password", "secret");        Connection connection =          DriverManager.getConnection(mySqlUrl, userInfo);     &#x2022; Optionally, look up info about the database         DatabaseMetaData dbMetaData =           connection.getMetaData();         String productName =           dbMetaData.getDatabaseProductName();         System.out.println("Database: " + productName);         String productVersion =           dbMetaData.getDatabaseProductVersion();         System.out.println("Version: " + productVersion);16 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-15-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 15 image" target="_blank">
        15.
      </a>
    JDBC Step 4: Make a Statement     &#x2022; Idea       &#x2013; A Statement is used to send queries or commands     &#x2022; Statement types       &#x2013; Statement, PreparedStatement, CallableStatement          &#x2022; Details on other types given later     &#x2022; Example       Statement statement =        connection.createStatement();17 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-16-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 16 image" target="_blank">
        16.
      </a>
    JDBC Step 5: Execute a Query     &#x2022; Idea       &#x2013; statement.executeQuery("SELECT &#x2026; FROM &#x2026;");            &#x2022; This version returns a ResultSet       &#x2013;   statement.executeUpdate("UPDATE &#x2026;");       &#x2013;   statement.executeUpdate("INSERT &#x2026;");       &#x2013;   statement.executeUpdate("DELETE&#x2026;");       &#x2013;   statement.execute("CREATE TABLE&#x2026;");       &#x2013;   statement.execute("DROP TABLE &#x2026;");     &#x2022; Example           String query =             "SELECT col1, col2, col3 FROM sometable";            ResultSet resultSet =              statement.executeQuery(query);18 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-17-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 17 image" target="_blank">
        17.
      </a>
    JDBC Step 6: Process the     Result     &#x2022; Important ResultSet methods       &#x2013; resultSet.next()          &#x2022; Goes to the next row. Returns false if no next row.       &#x2013; resultSet.getString("columnName")          &#x2022; Returns value of column with designated name in current            row, as a String. Also getInt, getDouble, getBlob, etc.       &#x2013; resultSet.getString(columnIndex)          &#x2022; Returns value of designated column. First index is 1 (ala            SQL), not 0 (ala Java).       &#x2013; resultSet.beforeFirst()          &#x2022; Moves cursor before first row, as it was initially. Also first       &#x2013; resultSet.absolute(rowNum)          &#x2022; Moves cursor to given row (starting with 1). Also last and            afterLast.19 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-18-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 18 image" target="_blank">
        18.
      </a>
    JDBC Step 6: Process the     Result     &#x2022; Assumption       &#x2013; Query was &#x201C;SELECT first, last, address FROM&#x2026;&#x201D;     &#x2022; Using column names        while(resultSet.next()) {          System.out.printf(            "First name: %s, last name: %s, address: %s%n",            resultSet.getString("first"),            resultSet.getString("last"),            resultSet.getString("address"));        }     &#x2022; Using column indices        while(resultSet.next()) {          System.out.printf(            "First name: %s, last name: %s, address: %s%n",            resultSet.getString(1),            resultSet.getString(2),20          resultSet.getString(3)); } 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-19-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 19 image" target="_blank">
        19.
      </a>
    JDBC Step 7: Close the     Connection     &#x2022; Idea       &#x2013; When totally done, close the database connection.         However, opening a new connection is typically much         more expensive than sending queries on existing         connections, so postpone this step as long as possible.       &#x2013; Many JDBC drivers do automatic connection pooling       &#x2013; There are also many explicit connection pool utilities     &#x2022; Example       connection.close();21 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-20-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 20 image" target="_blank">
        20.
      </a>
    &#xA9; 2012 Marty Hall   Using Apache Derby               Customized Java EE Training: http://courses.coreservlets.com/Java, JSF 2, PrimeFaces, Servlets, JSP, Ajax, jQuery, Spring, Hibernate, RESTful Web Services, Hadoop, Android. Developed and taught by well-known author and developer. At public venues or onsite at your location. 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-21-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 21 image" target="_blank">
        21.
      </a>
    Apache Derby: Overview     &#x2022; Overview       &#x2013; Written in Java. Good for small/medium applications         (less than gigabyte database size, few queries/second)       &#x2013; Bundled with Java 6, but latest version can be         downloaded from Apache for Java 1.4 and later.     &#x2022; Embedded mode       &#x2013; Database runs in same VM as Java app. Does not accept         network connections.       &#x2013; Perfect for Web apps          &#x2022; Incredibly easy to set up. Just drop in one JAR file          &#x2022; Good if database is accessed only from the Web apps     &#x2022; Standalone mode23       &#x2013; Runs in separate VM. Accepts network connections. 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-22-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 22 image" target="_blank">
        22.
      </a>
    Downloading and Installing     Derby     &#x2022; Downloading and documentation       &#x2013; http://db.apache.org/derby/     &#x2022; Use in embedded mode       &#x2013; Code          &#x2022; For Web apps, drop derby.jar in WEB-INF/lib          &#x2022; For other apps, put derby.jar in CLASSPATH       &#x2013; URL          &#x2022; jdbc:derby:databaseName       &#x2013; Driver class name          &#x2022; org.apache.derby.jdbc.EmbeddedDriver          &#x2022; Not needed in Java 6!       &#x2013; Username/password          &#x2022; Any are legal since DB runs inside the application.     &#x2022; Use in standalone mode       &#x2013; See http://db.apache.org/derby/papers/DerbyTut/       &#x2013; Consider MySQL, Oracle, etc. as alternatives24 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-23-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 23 image" target="_blank">
        23.
      </a>
    Setup Summary     &#x2022; Setup summary       &#x2013; Downloaded latest Derby ZIP from db.apache.org/derby/          &#x2022; db-derby-10.5.3.0-bin.zip, but any recent version is fine          &#x2022; You can also use version bundled with JDK 1.6.x       &#x2013; Unzipped       &#x2013; Put install_dir/lib/derby.jar into CLASSPATH          &#x2022; Many options in Eclipse, but if you make a Dynamic Web            Project, drop derby.jar in WebContent/WEB-INF/lib       &#x2013; That&#x2019;s it (for embedded usage)!          &#x2022; Compare this 90 second process to installing Oracle     &#x2022; Creating database       &#x2013; Can be created directly from Java using SQL commands         via JDBC. See later slides. Need to run creator code at         least once before accessing database.25 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-24-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 24 image" target="_blank">
        24.
      </a>
    Setup Details: Desktop Apps     &#x2022; Putting derby.jar in       CLASSPATH       &#x2013; R-click on project in Eclipse, create         new folder called &#x201C;lib&#x201D;. Put derby.jar         in lib.       &#x2013; R-click on project. Properties &#xF0E0; Java         Build Path &#xF0E0; Libraries &#xF0E0; Add JARs       &#x2013; Navigate to project/lib/ and select         derby.jar. Press OK.     &#x2022; Creating database       &#x2013; Manually run database creation code.         See &#x201C;Prepared Statements&#x201D; section for         code, but this needs to be done once         only. In most real apps, you have to         query database, but someone else26         creates the database. 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-25-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 25 image" target="_blank">
        25.
      </a>
    Setup Details: Web Apps     &#x2022; Putting derby.jar in CLASSPATH       &#x2013; Copy derby.jar to WEB-INF/lib     &#x2022; Creating database       &#x2013; Run database creation code. See &#x201C;Prepared Statements&#x201D;         section for code . This needs to be done once only, so best         way is to do it automatically in ServletContextListener. In         most real apps, you have to query database, but someone         else creates the database.          &#x2022; Reminder: full code can be downloaded from            http://courses.coreservlets.com/Course-Materials/            msajsp.html, so you can get db creation code there.27 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-26-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 26 image" target="_blank">
        26.
      </a>

    Employee Info Servlet     (Continued)     protected void showTable(PrintWriter out) {        try {          Connection connection = getConnection();          Statement statement = connection.createStatement();          String query = "SELECT * FROM " + tableName;          ResultSet resultSet = statement.executeQuery(query);          printTableTop(connection, resultSet, out);          printTableBody(resultSet, out);          connection.close();        } catch(Exception e) {          System.err.println("Error: " + e);        }      }41

    Employee Info Servlet      (Continued)      protected void printTableBody(ResultSet resultSet,                                     PrintWriter out)           throws SQLException {         // Step through each row in the result set and print cells         while(resultSet.next()) {           out.println("&lt;TR ALIGN=RIGHT&gt;");           out.printf(" &lt;TD&gt;%d", resultSet.getInt("id"));           out.printf(" &lt;TD&gt;%s", resultSet.getString("firstname"));           out.printf(" &lt;TD&gt;%s", resultSet.getString("lastname"));           out.printf(" &lt;TD&gt;%s", resultSet.getString("position"));           out.printf(" &lt;TD&gt;$%,d%n", resultSet.getInt("salary"));         }         out.println("&lt;/TABLE&gt;");       }     }44

    Using MetaData     &#x2022; Idea       &#x2013; For most queries, you know column names and database         version ahead of time. But you can discover this         dynamically as well.     &#x2022; System-wide data       &#x2013; connection.getMetaData().getDatabaseProductName()       &#x2013; connection.getMetaData().getDatabaseProductVersion()     &#x2022; Table-specific data       &#x2013; resultSet.getMetaData().getColumnCount()          &#x2022; When using the result, remember that            the index starts at 1, not 0       &#x2013; resultSet.getMetaData().getColumnName()47

    Using MetaData: Example     public class EmployeeServlet2 extends EmployeeServlet1 {       protected void printTableTop(Connection connection,                                    ResultSet resultSet,                                    PrintWriter out)           throws SQLException {         // Look up info about the database as a whole.         DatabaseMetaData dbMetaData = connection.getMetaData();         String productName =           dbMetaData.getDatabaseProductName();         String productVersion =           dbMetaData.getDatabaseProductVersion();         out.println("&lt;UL&gt;n" +                    " &lt;LI&gt;&lt;B&gt;Database:&lt;/B&gt;n" + productName +                    " &lt;LI&gt;&lt;B&gt;Version:&lt;/B&gt;n" + productVersion +                    "&lt;/UL&gt;");48

    Using MetaData: Example         (Continued)             out.println("&lt;TABLE BORDER=1&gt;");             // Discover and print headings             ResultSetMetaData resultSetMetaData =               resultSet.getMetaData();             int columnCount = resultSetMetaData.getColumnCount();             out.println("&lt;TR&gt;");             // Column index starts at 1 (a la SQL), not 0 (a la Java).             for(int i=1; i &lt;= columnCount; i++) {               out.printf("&lt;TH&gt;%s", resultSetMetaData.getColumnName(i));             }             out.println();         }     }49

    &#xA9; 2012 Marty Hall                Using Prepared                  Statements(Parameterized Commands)               Customized Java EE Training: http://courses.coreservlets.com/Java, JSF 2, PrimeFaces, Servlets, JSP, Ajax, jQuery, Spring, Hibernate, RESTful Web Services, Hadoop, Android. Developed and taught by well-known author and developer. At public venues or onsite at your location.

      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-50-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 50 image" target="_blank">
        50.
      </a>
    Overview     &#x2022; Situation       &#x2013; You are repeatedly executing query or update where         format stays consistent, but values change       &#x2013; You can make a parameterized query or update, then pass         in values for the placeholders     &#x2022; Advantages       &#x2013; More convenient than string concatenation       &#x2013; Significantly faster with most drivers and databases       &#x2013; If values contain user data, much less susceptible to SQL         injection attacks52         From Randall Munroe and xkcd.com 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-51-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 51 image" target="_blank">
        51.
      </a>
    Steps     &#x2022; Make a placeholder       &#x2013; Assume someTable has two columns (int and String)          String template =            "INSERT INTO someTable VALUES(?, ?)";          PreparedStatement inserter =             connection.prepareStatement(template);     &#x2022; Substitute in values       &#x2013; Use setInt(index), setString(index), etc. Remember         indices start with 1, not 0.          for(&#x2026;) {            inserter.setInt(1, someInt);            inserter.setString(2, someString)          }     &#x2022; Execute command          &#x2022; inserter.executeUpdate();53 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-52-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 52 image" target="_blank">
        52.
      </a>
    Creating the Database     &#x2022; Roles       &#x2013; Most JDBC developers do not need to create the database       &#x2013; That is the job of the database system admin     &#x2022; Apache Derby       &#x2013; You can run Derby-specific scripts and create the         database interactively       &#x2013; Or, you can use Java and JDBC          &#x2022; Using PreparedStatement simplifies the process     &#x2022; Simple &#x201C;myDatabase&#x201D; example       &#x2013; Created with Java and JDBC       &#x2013; Triggered from a ServletContextListener so database         creation code is executed at least once54 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-53-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 53 image" target="_blank">
        53.
      </a>
    Creating Sample Database     public class EmbeddedDbCreator {       // Driver class not needed in JDBC 4.0 (Java SE 6)       // private String driver =       //   "org.apache.derby.jdbc.EmbeddedDriver";       private String protocol = "jdbc:derby:";       private String username = "someuser";       private String password = "somepassword";       private String dbName = "myDatabase";       private String tableName = "employees";       private Properties userInfo;      public EmbeddedDbCreator() {        userInfo = new Properties();        userInfo.put("user", username);        userInfo.put("password", password);      }55

      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-54-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 54 image" target="_blank">
        54.

    Creating Sample Database     (Continued)     public void createDatabase() {       Employee[] employees = {          new Employee(1, "Larry", "Ellison", "CEO",                       1234567890),          new Employee(2, "Charles", "Phillips", "President",                       23456789),          new Employee(3, "Safra", "Catz", "President",                       32654987),          &#x2026;       };56

      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-55-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 55 image" target="_blank">
        55.
      </a>
    Creating Sample Database     (Continued)     try {             String dbUrl = protocol + dbName + ";create=true";             Connection connection =               DriverManager.getConnection(dbUrl, userInfo);             Statement statement = connection.createStatement();             String format = "VARCHAR(20)";             String tableDescription =               String.format                 ("CREATE TABLE %s" +                     "(id INT, firstname %s, lastname %s, " +                               "position %s, salary INT)",                    tableName, format, format, format);             statement.execute(tableDescription);57 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-56-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 56 image" target="_blank">
        56.
      </a>
    Creating Sample Database     (Continued)       String template =         String.format("INSERT INTO %s VALUES(?, ?, ?, ?, ?)",                       tableName);       PreparedStatement inserter =         connection.prepareStatement(template);       for(Employee e: employees) {         inserter.setInt(1, e.getEmployeeID());         inserter.setString(2, e.getFirstName());         inserter.setString(3, e.getLastName());         inserter.setString(4, e.getPosition());         inserter.setInt(5, e.getSalary());         inserter.executeUpdate();         System.out.printf("Inserted %s %s.%n",                           e.getFirstName(),                           e.getLastName());       }       inserter.close();       connection.close();58 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-57-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 57 image" target="_blank">
        57.
      </a>
    Triggering Database Creation     &#x2022; Database needs to be created once       &#x2013; Not for every request       &#x2013; Not even for every time server restarts     &#x2022; Goal       &#x2013; Create table when Web app is loaded          &#x2022; try/catch block in creation code halts process if table            already exists     &#x2022; Possible approaches       &#x2013; Servlet with creation code in init, and web.xml with         &lt;load-on-startup&gt;1&lt;/load-on-startup&gt;       &#x2013; ServletContextListener          &#x2022; Same effect as above, but more straightforward59       &#x2013; For desktop apps, just manually run the code once. 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-58-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 58 image" target="_blank">
        58.
      </a>
    Triggering Database Creation:         Listener     package coreservlets;     import javax.servlet.*;     public class DatabaseInitializer            implements ServletContextListener {       public void contextInitialized(ServletContextEvent event) {         new EmbeddedDbCreator().createDatabase();       }         public void contextDestroyed(ServletContextEvent event) {}     }60 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-59-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 59 image" target="_blank">
        59.
      </a>
    Triggering Database Creation:         web.xml     &#x2026;         &lt;listener&gt;           &lt;listener-class&gt;             coreservlets.DatabaseInitializer           &lt;/listener-class&gt;         &lt;/listener&gt;61 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-60-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 60 image" target="_blank">
        60.
      </a>
    &#xA9; 2012 Marty Hall      Advanced Features               Customized Java EE Training: http://courses.coreservlets.com/Java, JSF 2, PrimeFaces, Servlets, JSP, Ajax, jQuery, Spring, Hibernate, RESTful Web Services, Hadoop, Android. Developed and taught by well-known author and developer. At public venues or onsite at your location. 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-61-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 61 image" target="_blank">
        61.
      </a>
    Transactions     &#x2022; Idea       &#x2013; By default, after each SQL statement is executed the         changes are automatically committed to the database       &#x2013; Turn auto-commit off to group two or more statements         together into a transaction          connection.setAutoCommit(false);       &#x2013; Call commit to permanently record the changes to the         database after executing a group of statements       &#x2013; Call rollback if an error occurs63 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-62-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 62 image" target="_blank">
        62.
      </a>
    Transactions: Example     Connection connection =       DriverManager.getConnection(url, userProperties);     connection.setAutoCommit(false);     try {       statement.executeUpdate(...);       statement.executeUpdate(...);       ...       connection.commit();     } catch (Exception e) {       try {         connection.rollback();       } catch (SQLException sqle) {         // report problem       }     } finally {       try {        connection.close();       } catch (SQLException sqle) { }     }64 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-63-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 63 image" target="_blank">
        63.
      </a>
    Useful Connection Methods     (for Transactions)     &#x2022; getAutoCommit/setAutoCommit       &#x2013; By default, a connection is set to auto-commit       &#x2013; Retrieves or sets the auto-commit mode     &#x2022; commit       &#x2013; Force all changes since the last call to commit to become         permanent       &#x2013; Any database locks currently held by this Connection         object are released     &#x2022; rollback       &#x2013; Drops all changes since the previous call to commit       &#x2013; Releases any database locks held by this Connection         object65 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-64-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 64 image" target="_blank">
        64.
      </a>
    Using JNDI and DataSource     &#x2022; Idea       &#x2013; Use abstract name to get connection from a data source     &#x2022; Advantages       &#x2013; Lets you change data source without changing code       &#x2013; Available in multiple Web apps for network databases         (not embedded Derby!)     &#x2022; Disadvantage       &#x2013; Requires server-specific registration of data source     &#x2022; Code for steps 1-3 replaced by:       Context context = new InitialContext();       DataSource dataSource = (DataSource)context.lookup                          ("java:comp/env/jdbc/dbName");       Connection connection = dataSource.getConnection();66 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-65-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 65 image" target="_blank">
        65.
      </a>
    DataSource: Tomcat Configuration      (META-INF/context.xml)     &lt;?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?&gt;     &lt;Context&gt;       &lt;Resource          name="jdbc/myDatabase"          driverClassName="org.apache.derby.jdbc.ClientDriver"          url="jdbc:derby:myDatabase"          type="javax.sql.DataSource"          username="someuser"          password="somepassword"          auth="Container"          maxActive="8" /&gt;     &lt;/Context&gt;67 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-66-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 66 image" target="_blank">
        66.
      </a>
    More JDBC Options     &#x2022;   Stored procedures     &#x2022;   Changing buffer size     &#x2022;   Connection pooling     &#x2022;   Hibernate/JPA and other ORM tools          &#x2013; See tutorials at coreservlets.com     &#x2022; JSP Standard Tag Library (JSTL)          &#x2013; Custom tags to hide JDBC details.             &#x2022; Some developers use JSTL to loop down the ResultSet.               Disadvantage: ties presentation layer to JDBC.             &#x2022; Some developers use JSTL to actually do queries. Simple.               Disadvantage: very inflexible and violates MVC principle.68 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-67-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 67 image" target="_blank">
        67.
      </a>
    &#xA9; 2012 Marty Hall                               Wrap-Up               Customized Java EE Training: http://courses.coreservlets.com/Java, JSF 2, PrimeFaces, Servlets, JSP, Ajax, jQuery, Spring, Hibernate, RESTful Web Services, Hadoop, Android. Developed and taught by well-known author and developer. At public venues or onsite at your location. 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-68-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 68 image" target="_blank">
        68.
      </a>
    JDBC and Derby References     &#x2022; Books       &#x2013; JDBC API Tutorial and Reference by Maydene         Fisher, Jon Ellis, and Jonathan Bruce (Prentice Hall)       &#x2013; Expert Oracle JDBC Programming by R.M. Menon         (APress)       &#x2013; JDBC Recipes: A Problem-Solution Approach by         Mahmoud Parsian (APress)     &#x2022; Sun JDBC tutorial       &#x2013; http://java.sun.com/docs/books/tutorial/jdbc/     &#x2022; Derby references       &#x2013; Derby beginner&#x2019;s tutorial          &#x2022; http://db.apache.org/derby/papers/DerbyTut/       &#x2013; Derby 10.4 manuals          &#x2022; http://db.apache.org/derby/manuals/index.html#docs_10.470 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-69-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 69 image" target="_blank">
        69.
      </a>
    Summary     1. Load the driver       &#x2013;   Not required in Java 6; use Class.forName otherwise     2. Define the Connection URL       &#x2013;   jdbc:vendor:blah (vendor gives exact format)     3. Establish the Connection       &#x2013;   DriverManager.getConnection     4. Create a Statement object       &#x2013;   connection.createStatement     5. Execute a query       &#x2013;   statement.executeQuery     6. Process the results       &#x2013;   Loop using resultSet.next()       &#x2013;   Call getString, getInt, etc.     7. Close the connection71 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/10-jdbc-120914151504-phpapp02/95/java-7-programming-tutorial-accessing-databases-with-jdbc-70-728.jpg?cb=1347635954" title="View slide 70 image" target="_blank">
        70.
      </a>
